  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_26d9ddc2-86a0-49c8-8c79-13ba361a4cee'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

Popular Answered Questions

<div id='communityQuestionsWithAnswers'>
<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1467854-can-no-one-hear-jenks-when-he-s-not">Can no one hear Jenks when he&#39;s not talking specifically to them? It just seems like he&#39;s very chatty in need-to-be-quiet situations. It also seems like he and Rachel chat about something in a plan when someone is near and they either are not listening to them talk about their plan, or there is something I&#39;m missing?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_1467854'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F30262.The_Good_the_Bad_and_the_Undead">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/1467854-can-no-one-hear-jenks-when-he-s-not">2 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/1467854-can-no-one-hear-jenks-when-he-s-not">See all 2 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/4592678-mel"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1463964245i/4592678._UY100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/4592678-mel">Mel</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Hello Crystal. I believe there is a combination of things going on here. First, Jenks is usually sitting on Rachel’s shoulder when he is making the ru<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Hello Crystal. I believe there is a combination of things going on here. First, Jenks is usually sitting on Rachel’s shoulder when he is making the rude comments or talking when he shouldn’t be. Perhaps, he is talking quietly enough that most would not hear him. Second, pixies have a magic that allows them to be understood. We discover this in Black Magic Sanction (Book 8) when she turns herself small and human sized people cannot understand her. Rachel makes high pitched squeaky sounds when she is pixie size because Ceri forgot to incorporated that into the charm. Maybe, Jenks is using his magic to ensure only she can hear him??? Finally, humans and other Inderlanders consider pixies to be not much more than bugs. They are looked down on by most. I believe many discriminate against pixies so they simply ignore him because they do not believe he has anything useful to say. I am currently re-listening to this series before I read American Demon. I come across your questions recently. I am not exactly sure what is the correct answer but these are my thoughts on your question as I re-listen. Take care and happy reading.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans?shelf=vamps-are-wimps">vamps-are-wimps</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans?shelf=demons-are-yummy">demons-are-yummy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1085758824" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13911747738058509296"><b><u>Actual rating</u>: 3.5 stars</b>.<br/><br/>Well well well, would you look at that?! It seems the <b>Freaking MacHalo TBR Cleaning Challenge of Doom and Destruction</b> (FMTCCoDaD™) isn't ALL about reading crap, after all! Who would have thought?! Not only did I NOT feel like <b>killing this book with fire</b>, but I actually enjoyed reading it *gasps* Despite its <b>Disaster Waiting to Happen Ingredients</b> (DWtHI™)! Wow. Imagine that!<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1449477305ra/17290815.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Flabbergastation is me</b> <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[
  <i>yes, flabbergastation is a word. Just in case you were won</i></span></span>
  <span id="freeText13911747738058509296" style="display:none"><b><u>Actual rating</u>: 3.5 stars</b>.<br><br>Well well well, would you look at that?! It seems the <b>Freaking MacHalo TBR Cleaning Challenge of Doom and Destruction</b> (FMTCCoDaD™) isn't ALL about reading crap, after all! Who would have thought?! Not only did I NOT feel like <b>killing this book with fire</b>, but I actually enjoyed reading it *gasps* Despite its <b>Disaster Waiting to Happen Ingredients</b> (DWtHI™)! Wow. Imagine that!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1449477305ra/17290815.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Flabbergastation is me</b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <i>yes, flabbergastation is a word. Just in case you were wondering. You're welcome.</i>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I mean, I'm so used to reading UF rubbish these days, any Non-Crappy UF Object (NCUO™) I manage to get my hands on comes as a shock. Hence the <b>dramatic fainting and stuff</b>.<br><br><b>What</b>? You want me to cut the crap and get right down do the DWtHI™? Why? You don't think what I've been saying so far is <b>absolutely, totally and completely fascinating</b>? Okay, you know what, don't answer that one, I have a feeling I won't like what you have to say. But anyway. So you want do get <b>down and dirty with no foreplay</b>, huh? Sigh. You bunch of silly arthropods don't know what you are missing, but hey, it's your lives, so suit your little selves. <b>Express Crap Cutting</b> (ECC™), here we go.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452506561i/17699944.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So. Had I been my <b>normal, healthy, balanced, sensible self</b> when I read this story, I probably would have either rated it 2 stars or DNFed the shrimp out of it. Oh yes. Why? What do you mean "why?" <b>Because of the DWtHI™, of course</b>! Please do try to follow, my Little Barnacles, it would make my life a whole lot easier. Especially on days like this one, when you expect me to cut the freaking crap. So please <b>shut the shrimp up</b>, and let me try and to do this as quickly and painlessly as possible. <br><br><b>
  <u>There are two major DWtHI™ in this book</u>
</b>:<br><br>① Rachel Morgan is quite the <b>aspiring TSTL heroine</b> sometimes. <br><br>② Rachel Morgan has the <b>most boring boyfriend in the history of boring boyfriends</b>. <br><br><b>That's it? Yep, that's it</b>. What? You think these two little things alone are not reason enough to DNF the shrimp out of a book? Don't you know me at all? I've DNFed books <b>with less than one freaking DWtHI™</b> in the past, so believe me, my Lovely Arthropods, nothing is impossible in <b>Kill it with Fire Land</b> (KiwFL™).<br><br><b>So YES</b>, our dear Rachel has TSTL tendencies, but <b>I like her anyway</b>. And yes, she has a <b>Supremely Uninteresting, Slightly Annoying Boyfriend</b> (SUSAB™), but I'm fairly confident he will be <b>appropriately disposed of</b> in the next instalment, so all is well in the world. Or will be. Hopefully. Because if she Rachel doesn't ditch the guy soon, I shall gladly <b>take care of it for her</b>. Which loosely translates to mean: I'll chop him into tiny little pieces and <b>feed him to the murderous crustaceans</b> for the end of summer banquet. Ooooooh, I think my babies would definitely like that. <b>Yum yum yum and stuff</b>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473155531i/20417388._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Anyway, <b>the answer to the question you didn't ask is yes, by the way</b>. YES, I will continue with this series. Because it's <b>pretty cool and fun and entertaining</b>, despite the DWtHI™. Because the <b>story arc is pretty intriguing and stuff</b>. And because <b>Yummy Trent Kamalack is Yummy</b> (YTKiY™). And because <b>Jenks is the hottest pixy ever</b>. And I usually hate these suckers. Because pixies make me think of fairies and <b>Fairies are Silly Sissies</b> (FaSS™). But Jenks is Jenks. <b>So fatal attraction and all that crap</b>. Oh, and one more reason why YES, I shall continue with this series: because <b>demons are yummy</b>. But you already knew that. And even if you didn't, just pretend you did. Good Little Barnacles. <b>Daddy is so proud of you right now</b>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451576569ra/17560318.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>» <b>And the moral of this Express Crap Cutting Non Review</b> (ECCNR™) is: contrary to popular belief, I can be reasonable sometimes, and <b>choose to overlook stuff I choose to overlook</b>. Because if I didn't choose to overlook stuff I choose to overlook, I'd probably end up DNFing 99.99% of the books I <s>DNF</s> <s>try to</s> read. <b>Ha</b>.<br><br>· <b>Book 1</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1078123571" rel="nofollow noopener">Dead Witch Walking</a> ★★<br>· <b>Book 3</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1731058064" rel="nofollow noopener">Every Which Way But Dead</a> ★★</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_49885695" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/49885695" />
    <a title="Robin Wiley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2140942-robin-wiley"><img alt="Robin Wiley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1239062598p2/2140942.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/49885695?book_show_action=true">Mar 20, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin Wiley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin Wiley" href="/user/show/2140942-robin-wiley">Robin Wiley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer49885695" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12311286163850966962">I've read most of the majors in this genre: Stoker, Rice, Harrison, Harris, King, Hamilton, Meyer, Newman, and Kostova. I've seen Blade, Underworld, Buffy, Angel, Van Helsing, 30 Days of Night, Moonlight and Dark Shadows (not saying they are all good, mind you). So, I think I've consumed enough of the vampire genre to have some opinions.<br/><br/>My theory about Twilight. People with little to no experience with the vampire genre LOVE this series. Most readers who have consumed their fair amount of vampir</span>
  <span id="freeText12311286163850966962" style="display:none">I've read most of the majors in this genre: Stoker, Rice, Harrison, Harris, King, Hamilton, Meyer, Newman, and Kostova. I've seen Blade, Underworld, Buffy, Angel, Van Helsing, 30 Days of Night, Moonlight and Dark Shadows (not saying they are all good, mind you). So, I think I've consumed enough of the vampire genre to have some opinions.<br /><br />My theory about Twilight. People with little to no experience with the vampire genre LOVE this series. Most readers who have consumed their fair amount of vampire genre - not so much. Somebody do a poll, quick, and prove me right.<br /><br />So why is Harrison great?<br /><br />Rachel Morgan is a sassy, sarcastic, kick-ass witch. Forget pointy hats, brooms and wands. Think leather pants, sexy boots and charms cooked up in a modern day kitchen. When charms don't work, a throat punch or round house kick will do. She's a bounty hunter who hunts down the bad guys - who are mostly non-human.<br /><br />Because of a genetically engineered tomato gone bad - half the world population died of food poisoning (basically). That's when the witches, werewolves, and vampires came out of the closet. Laws were formed to accomodate the different populations. Our girl s with the police for non-humans against human crimes, then she leaves because things go terribly and horribly wrong.<br /><br />It reads very Joss Whedon. Sarcastic banter. Kick ass fight scenes. The vampire "rules" are good - they make sense for modern day vamps in a modern society. <br /><br />What's to love?<br /><br />ACTION - great!<br />MAGIC - good, different, makes sense, solid (I liked Harry Potter, but I like non-wand magic alot more)<br />HUMOR - if you like Joss Whedon - you have to read this.<br />CREATURES - there's more species than the three I've named. 'Nuf said.<br /><br />What's not so fun?<br /><br />That you're not already reading it!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12311286163850966962" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer351709081" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2744386781702641734"><b>2/7/18 - ON SALE for $3.99:</b><br/><br/><a href='https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B000FC2RRC/ref=as_li_ss_il?ie=UTF8&linkCode=li1&tag=rabrea-20&linkId=9b69d324b42ed5a6cc4496019caa3cda' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1425400420i/13884348.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1517578913i/24989193.gif' width='1' height='1' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://amzn.to/2E6K3VD'>http://amzn.to/2E6K3VD</a><br/><br/><b>Reviewed by: <a href='http://rabidreads.ca/2014/05/review-the-good-the-bad-and-the-undead.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rabid Reads</a></b><br/><br/>If I still had any doubts about <em>The Hollows</em> when I finished the <em>Dead Witch Walking</em>, <em>The Good, the Bad, and the Undead</em> laid them to rest.<br/><br/>Book 2 begins with Rachel and Jenks in the middle of a run. Several months has passed since the first book ended, and without a death threat hanging over her head, Rachel is free to pursue her new career as an independent runner. Nick is now officially Rachel's boyfriend, and the roomma</span>
  <span id="freeText2744386781702641734" style="display:none"><b>2/7/18 - ON SALE for $3.99:</b><br><br><a href="https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B000FC2RRC/ref=as_li_ss_il?ie=UTF8&amp;linkCode=li1&amp;tag=rabrea-20&amp;linkId=9b69d324b42ed5a6cc4496019caa3cda" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1425400420i/13884348.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1517578913i/24989193.gif" width="1" height="1" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://amzn.to/2E6K3VD">http://amzn.to/2E6K3VD</a><br><br><b>Reviewed by: <a href="http://rabidreads.ca/2014/05/review-the-good-the-bad-and-the-undead.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabid Reads</a></b><br><br>If I still had any doubts about <em>The Hollows</em> when I finished the <em>Dead Witch Walking</em>, <em>The Good, the Bad, and the Undead</em> laid them to rest.<br><br>Book 2 begins with Rachel and Jenks in the middle of a run. Several months has passed since the first book ended, and without a death threat hanging over her head, Rachel is free to pursue her new career as an independent runner. Nick is now officially Rachel's boyfriend, and the roommate situation with Ivy seems to have calmed down now that Rachel knows what Ivy's triggers are and not to pull them.<br><br>And things just keep swimming merrily along. (&lt;-----did you see what I did there? *snickers*)<br><br>Riiiiiight . . .<br><br>Even if (for some strange reason) you were hoping things would calm down for our new favorite witch, when Glenn shows up as Rachel and Jenks' ride after the run (instead of Ivy), and insists on taking a detour to the FIB (Federal Inderland Bureau---the human version of police enforcement), it seems HIGHLY unlikely.<br><br>Even MORE unlikely when you learn the reason for the detour is that Sarah Jane (Trent's new secretary) is there being questioned after reporting her missing boyfriend.<br><br>A serial killer is on the loose in Cincinnati, you see. And serial killers have VERY particular tastes. This one has been viciously murdering ley line witches . . . and guess what Sarah Jane's boyfriend happens to be . . .<br><br>SO many things happen in this book.<br><br>Rachel shows an uncommon aptitude for ley line witchcraft. This is distressing for her, b/c as she has stated (on numerous occasions) she is <em>strictly</em> an earth witch. Ley line magic isn't as black and white as earth magic, and Rachel has seen too many friends slide down that slippery slope from white, to gray, to black b/c POWER lurks in ley line magic. POWER that tempts and overwhelms, and Rachel wants no part of it.<br><br>We find out what Trent is. Not telling. READ IT. *poke*<br><br>Rachel discovers links between her father and the Kalamacks. Not telling that either. *pokes again*<br><br>And <em>not</em> lastly (not by a long shot, but if I were to list all of the Big Deal things that happened in this book, we'd be here all day, AND I'd probably get smacked from all the poking), Rachel makes a deal with a demon that sets up for book 3 rather nicely. And by "nicely" I mean "holycraphowisshegoingtogetoutofthatone?!"<br><br>In addition to SO many things happening in this book, SO many characters are further developed and/or introduced.<br><br>We meet Rachel's wacky mother (who accidentally alludes to a HUGE secret that gets revealed later on), and Piscary (hey, I just noticed "scary" is in his name . . . wonder if that was on purpose . . . hmmm . . . ), the <em>scary</em> master vamp. We also meet the several times mentioned, but never actually seen Quen (one of my favorite secondaries). Trent is shown in a less diabolical light that makes him a much more complicated individual, and Nick . . . well, Nick's moral code is revealed to be even more nebulous than previously suspected, but due to certain other events, I can't help but feel a bit sorry for him. That whole situation is just a MESS.<br><br>And again MORE. Too much to cover all of it, but believe me when I say that it was very well done.<br><br>There wasn't much on the world-building front, but then it wasn't really necessary. Pretty  much everything you need to know was covered in the first book. I still find it slightly ridiculous every time Rachel goes out of her way to hide evidence of tomato consumption from the humans, but what are you going to do?<br><br>Tomato ridiculousness aside, <em>The Good, the Bad, and the Undead</em> brilliantly avoided the book 2 slump that so many series fall prey to. It was another artful combination of humor, action, danger, and flirtation, and BONUS all of this took place within a well-developed and identifiable plot! I know! It so rarely happens that I don't know what to do either!<br><br>That's not true, I know exactly what to do---read the next book. *wink*<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421060968i/13316940.jpg" alt="Jessica Signature" width="205" height="101" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>My other reviews for this series:</b><br><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/351599255" rel="nofollow noopener">Dead Witch Walking (The Hollows #1)</a>
</b><br><b>

  <span id="freeText6803643651658942141" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/759082039?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Dead Witch Walking</a>: ★★★★<br /><br />SECOND READ: ★★★★★<br />FIRST READ: ★★★ <br /><br />Buddy read with the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148935-the-machalo-asylum-for-mischief-and-mayhem-mam" rel="nofollow noopener">MacHalos</a>.<br /><br />Wow! I'm so excited to be re-reading this. I liked it much better the second time around. This one is mainly about the vampires and Rachel discovering ley line magic.<br /><br />Al is the absolute best. I remembered the plot, but it was still very fresh to me. I actually have a lot more sympathy for Ivy this time around and am liking her much more.<br /><br />You know, Rachel IS annoying, but it works for me. She's so stupid sometimes, bratty, but when she fails or gets in trouble, she KNOWS it's her own fault. She just has a big mouth and an alpha type personality, even if she doesn't know HOW to be an alpha. I kind of find her bumbling around refreshing.<br /><br />Kisten is bae, just as he was the first time around. Piscary is scary. Huh, his name has the word scary in it. He's a good classic villain type. I hate him.<br /><br />I am actually liking Trent a lot more this time around too.<br /><br />I'm pretty much just going to jump right into book three! </span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=super-sidekicks">super-sidekicks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=kick-ass-heroines">kick-ass-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=witches-warlocks-and-magic">witches-warlocks-and-magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=uf-pnr">uf-pnr</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1076768560" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12752149372366245083">Rachel Mariana Morgan, you are the character in the movie that I yell at. That I scream at <i>“Don’t go into that empty warehouse! Don’t practice spells you know nothing about! Never talk with Demons!!!”</i> But does she listen NOOOO….No wonder she is always in some sort of crisis.<br/><br/>Rachel isn’t my favorite heroine and normally that would be enough to steer me away from a series but I really enjoy all the other parts of the series. There is enough humor, mystery and other interesting characters to keep m</span>
  <span id="freeText12752149372366245083" style="display:none">Rachel Mariana Morgan, you are the character in the movie that I yell at. That I scream at <i>“Don’t go into that empty warehouse! Don’t practice spells you know nothing about! Never talk with Demons!!!”</i> But does she listen NOOOO….No wonder she is always in some sort of crisis.<br /><br />Rachel isn’t my favorite heroine and normally that would be enough to steer me away from a series but I really enjoy all the other parts of the series. There is enough humor, mystery and other interesting characters to keep me engaged even when I want to scream at Rachel. <br /><br />A few things in this book I really enjoyed were her developing relationship with Nick, which let’s face it now is probably doomed and not just because he is a human and Rachel’s mom loves him…<br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“I like you. Marry Rachel and have lots of kids.”<br />“Mom!” I exclaimed. Nick grinned, enjoying it.<br />“But not right away,” she continued. “Enjoy your freedom together for a while. You don’t want children until you’re ready. You are practicing safe sex, yes?”<br />“Mother!” I shouted. “Shut up!” God, help me get through this night.<br />She turned, one hand on her hip, the other holding the dripping spoon. “Rachel, if you didn’t want me to bring it up, you should have spelled your hickey.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br />But also because of a little/big thing Rtachel did in this book and a demon. Still I enjoyed their time on page together and their continueing relationship will be interesting if nothing else.<br /><br />The backstory development was really good too. We find out what Trent is, what his connection to Rachel is and a little bit of what her father was into. And then there is Ivy and that whole situation. It seems that everyone seems to see Ivy’s motives aren’t entirely pure except Rachel.<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“She wants something,” he said. “And every time she looks at you, I see guilt. Whether she means to or not, she’s going to hurt you, and she knows it.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />I now have a little better understanding of Ivy’s plans for Rachel and while I’m not on board with them I could see the draw.<br /><br /><b>There are exactly 2 reasons I’m going to continue this series. Trent and Big Al</b><br /><br />Finding out what Trent is and part of his connection to Rachel was just a taste. I’m sure and I really want to find out even more about this guy who seems to be a little bit good, a little bit bad and smoldering hot. Big Al on the other hand is probably all bad but in the best way, blame it on the Demon thing if you must. He is tricky and he has gotten the best of Rachel two times now, I have no idea how she will get out of this mess.<br /><br />The storyline of the serial killer of Ley Line witches was interesting and wrapped up pretty well, but overall I’m more interesting in the overlapping plot arcs that will go on throughout the series, especially those centering on Rachel’s Dad and Big Al.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12752149372366245083" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_265353154" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/265353154" />
    <a title="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence"><img alt="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559561558p2/6186603.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/265353154?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " href="/user/show/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence">Jeann (Happy Indulgence) </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence?shelf=witches">witches</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence?shelf=paranormal-uf">paranormal-uf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence?shelf=dark-and-gritty">dark-and-gritty</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer265353154" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13323063499773572938">The second book in the Hollows series is written much better than the haphazard style of Dead Witch Walking. I'm glad I stuck with the series because it's a really unique and interesting one. Firstly, it seems like the author has done with some good editing and slowly interweaves the world building with what is happening at the time, instead of having huge info dumps at random intervals. <br/><br/>Rachel Morgan slowly learns to stand on her own and develop her powers further in this book. As an FIB consul</span>
  <span id="freeText13323063499773572938" style="display:none">The second book in the Hollows series is written much better than the haphazard style of Dead Witch Walking. I'm glad I stuck with the series because it's a really unique and interesting one. Firstly, it seems like the author has done with some good editing and slowly interweaves the world building with what is happening at the time, instead of having huge info dumps at random intervals. <br /><br />Rachel Morgan slowly learns to stand on her own and develop her powers further in this book. As an FIB consultant, she's assisting in a murder investigation using her strong intuition and witchy powers. The host of side characters such as Ivy, Nick, and Jenks are developed further and they are complex characters so it's interesting to follow.<br /><br />There's some interesting developments to follow in this book, and I especially find entertaining how tomatoes are feared by all humans due to them containing a virus that wiped out 1/4 of humanity. This book is multi-layered and has complex characters and developments, and it is easily enjoyable. <br /><br />I recommend The Hollows series to anyone who hasn't started it yet, and keen to start on the next one.<br /><br /><a href="http://www.happyindulgencebooks.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Check out Happy Indulgence for more reviews!</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13323063499773572938" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2165070714" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15924849417843186113">Hmmm. This is definitely better than the first. There’s something quite compelling about this series. This confuses me though as there are some annoyances too. I found the plot a little convoluted and I don’t like Nick much. Also the main character Rachel is pretty annoying a lot of the time. Still. I’ve given better books a lower rating on occasion. Go figure!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1177586163" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1177586163" />
    <a title="Lazaros" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22313662-lazaros"><img alt="Lazaros" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578697302p2/22313662.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1177586163?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lazaros" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lazaros" href="/user/show/22313662-lazaros">Lazaros</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007459766" href="/book/show/12973305-the-good-the-bad-and-the-undead">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">urban fantasy lovers</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=girl-power">girl-power</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=witches">witches</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1177586163" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2798040085487779160">I'll say it again. If you're fan of a good read with amazing characters with snarky retorts and sassy attitudes and you love yourself some action-packed urban fantasy then don't hesitate, do read this. I am most pleased by how this book turned out. It was a nice surprise that it kept getting better than the first novel and I actually liked it even more. Since I gave the first book 5 stars it's only fair that I give this 5 stars as well.<br/><br/>There is a little bit more romance in this one. If you remem</span>
  <span id="freeText2798040085487779160" style="display:none">I'll say it again. If you're fan of a good read with amazing characters with snarky retorts and sassy attitudes and you love yourself some action-packed urban fantasy then don't hesitate, do read this. I am most pleased by how this book turned out. It was a nice surprise that it kept getting better than the first novel and I actually liked it even more. Since I gave the first book 5 stars it's only fair that I give this 5 stars as well.<br /><br />There is a little bit more romance in this one. If you remember Nick from the first book, well, he's Rachel's boyfriend and their relationship is kind of cute to read and I kind of like them together but to be honest I wouldn't mind if they seperated. <br /><br />There is a witch hunter on the loose. More like a ley-witch hunter and Rachel, Jenks &amp; Ivy (from time to time) help the FIB, along with Glenn (Edden's son) to find out and apprehend the killer. Not surprisingly all eyes turn to Trent and Rachel tries to incriminate him for the killings and watch him going down.<br /><br />There are twists, many of them. There is tention between our characters &amp; lots of unpredictability, which I liked a lot. Our characters aren't simple, they're complicated and they have problems and they're trying to work through them. I'm glad that this book changed my opinion about Rachel, which I grew to love in this one. In the first book I liked her but didn't quite find her as fascinating as I thought she would be. Ivy is still one hell of a vamp and I adore her and I hate how she's struggling and faces everything on her own. I want her friends to stand up for her, finally!<br /><br />This book was so fun, fun, fun. There is drama but all the fun drowns out the drama and I had a great time reading it, laughing and snorting. There is so much action, there's always action and it'll come right when you didn't expect it. <br /><br />Can't wait to dive into the next book and devour it like I did this one. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2798040085487779160" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_337571145" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/337571145" />
    <a title="Jonetta" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4876540-jonetta"><img alt="Jonetta" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1329083158p2/4876540.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/337571145?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jonetta" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jonetta" href="/user/show/4876540-jonetta">Jonetta</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781400134724" href="/book/show/1352200.The_Good_the_Bad_and_the_Undead">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4876540-jonetta?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4876540-jonetta?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer337571145" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1868479970020595753">I got so bogged down by the world building of the first book I put the series on hiatus. This time I switched to the audio format and it turned out to be a brilliant move as the narrator, Marguerite Gavin, gives an inspired performance. <br/><br/>There are many lingering questions from Dead Witch Walking that are resolved in this story (what is Trent, who unleashed the demon on Rachel, who is Ivy really, etc.). And, some I had that are still outstanding but we get more info on, enough to whet the appetite</span>
  <span id="freeText1868479970020595753" style="display:none">I got so bogged down by the world building of the first book I put the series on hiatus. This time I switched to the audio format and it turned out to be a brilliant move as the narrator, Marguerite Gavin, gives an inspired performance. <br /><br />There are many lingering questions from Dead Witch Walking that are resolved in this story (what is Trent, who unleashed the demon on Rachel, who is Ivy really, etc.). And, some I had that are still outstanding but we get more info on, enough to whet the appetite. <br /><br />Ivy bugged me, a lot, in the first story and she got under my skin again in this one. However, by the end, I understand her more fully and why Rachel is so committed to the relationship. And, Nick...don't get me started on him. Still don't trust him and think there's quite a bit more to him than he lets on. Trent, well, he's the enigma that keeps on giving. <br /><br />There's a lot that works about this story, enough that I've dusted off the series and restored it to front row status. I'm grateful to friends who strongly urged me to keep going. It's a complex world with interesting characters and enough political intrigue to keep you completely off balance. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1868479970020595753" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Years ago, I read the first several books in this series but never went any further for some reason. I meant to but I guess I got distracted by other shiny books or something. Since I knew I need a refresher before moving on with the series, I thought that a re-read would be a perfect choice. I am almost positive that I liked it even better this time around.<br/><br/>This book starts with a bang. Rachel and Jenks are in t</span>
  <span id="freeText16342393724169348687" style="display:none">This review can also be found at <a href="http://carolesrandomlife.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Carole's Random Life</a>.<br /><br />This was such a fun audiobook! Years ago, I read the first several books in this series but never went any further for some reason. I meant to but I guess I got distracted by other shiny books or something. Since I knew I need a refresher before moving on with the series, I thought that a re-read would be a perfect choice. I am almost positive that I liked it even better this time around.<br /><br />This book starts with a bang. Rachel and Jenks are in the middle of a run....and things don't go as smoothly as they would have hoped. One thing leads to another and before you know it Rachel is in the middle of a much bigger case and has a new human sidekick to go with the gig. This book really has a lot packed into it with a pretty compelling mystery at the heart of the story. There are a lot of side plots that also keep the story moving.<br /><br />I love the characters. Rachel is just all kinds of awesome. I like she handles herself in really difficult situations. She keeps an even head and can think about things from different points of view. She also tries hard to do what is right. Jenks is nearly perfect. He is tough and always seems to add a lot to every scene he is a part of. Ivy is still a bit of a mystery but I like the tension she adds to story.<br /><br />Marguerite Gavin is the perfect choice for narrator with this series. She is somehow able to capture each of the different characters in this book flawlessly. Each character's voice was unique and fit their personality. I was able to stay completely focused on the story and had a hard time setting it aside to do anything else. I think that her narration really made the story come alive.<br /><br />I would highly recommend this series to fans of urban fiction. I do think that this is a series that really should be read in order since some of the story builds on previous books. I can't wait to move on to the next book in the series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16342393724169348687" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1330989274" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1330989274" />
    <a title="Obsidian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35942740-obsidian"><img alt="Obsidian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509845837p2/35942740.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1330989274?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Obsidian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Obsidian" href="/user/show/35942740-obsidian">Obsidian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1330989274" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10172521332867536926">This is my buddy read of the Hollows series with Moonlight Reader. <br/> <br/> <br/>As it stands I only like two characters at this point, and one of them is a murderer. The other characters are not smart, keep doing increasing dumb things, and are just awful. Besides the characters, the world building at this point makes no sense. We have another mythical creature coming out to play, and it makes no sense in the larger context of the world that Rachel lives in right now. Maybe if I cared enough I would have r</span>
  <span id="freeText10172521332867536926" style="display:none">This is my buddy read of the Hollows series with Moonlight Reader. <br /> <br /> <br />As it stands I only like two characters at this point, and one of them is a murderer. The other characters are not smart, keep doing increasing dumb things, and are just awful. Besides the characters, the world building at this point makes no sense. We have another mythical creature coming out to play, and it makes no sense in the larger context of the world that Rachel lives in right now. Maybe if I cared enough I would have re-read some passages. However, there comes a point when you just want to be done with a book. I hit that point around 12:30 a.m. <br /> <br />Told in the first person by Rachel Morgan, The Good, the Bad, and the Undead, still has Rachel reeling from the events in the first book. Now working alongside vampire Ivy as an independent agency, she is still focused on bringing down businessman Trent Kalamack. When some witch murders start popping up in Cincinnati, Rachel thinks this is her chance to tie the murders to Trent, and bring him to justice. <br /> <br />The plot should have been fairly simple, but there were all these other plots (B, C, and I think a D in there as well) that were supposed to be part of the larger plot, but ended up making everything hang together badly. We have Rachel investigating a missing case, that then ties into some witch murders, which leads to a revelation about a demon, which is kind of linked to why Ivy keeps hulking out on Rachel, which turns to Rachel finding out about a friendship her father had with someone she hates, which is the house that jack built. I am being facetious here, but seriously, it was a long winding road to the end. <br /> <br />It always sucks when you don't like the main character in the book you're reading. I really don't like Rachel at this point. Maybe it's because she's not that smart, and keeps apologizing to the wrong people when situations arise either of her own making or the other persons. And I can't stand to keep reading these books if every time Rachel gets out of sorts, it sets off Ivy, and then Ivy tries to feed on her by force and Rachel manages to save herself or someone else comes along and saves her. Long story short we have Rachel once again apologizing to Ivy once she vamps out and tries to force/kill Rachel. If it wasn't for Rachel's boyfriend Nick riding to the rescue, Rachel would be toast. And how does Rachel repay him?<br /> <br /><blockquote>Are you sure you're all right? he asked, his hand buried deep in my hair as he held me.<br />I pulled away to look at him. <br />Yes. Thanks. Where's Ivy?<br />He didn't say anything, and my face went slack in alarm. <br />She didn't hurt you, did she?<br />His hand dropped from my hair. <br />She's on the floor where I left her.<br />Nick! I protested, pushing myself away from him so I could sit straight.<br />How could you just leave her there?</blockquote><br /> <br />If Rachel was a real life person and I knew her, I would probably be arrested for shaking the life out of her. Seriously? You don't have a problem that for the third time in three months your roommate has tried to force you to accept her enough so she can bite you? Bah to you.<br /><br />And I honestly don't know what Ms. Harrison was going for her in the longer context of this novel. Rachel is like a 2 year old that can be distracted by a bright shiny thing. Every few seconds I felt like she was feeling drawn to someone else and she was in a relationship. The ending with her having some sort of revelation about what happened to some mythical creatures just made me roll my eyes. Even broken clocks are right twice a day. I am sure that is going to be followed up in some subsequent book. <br /> <br /> <br />Jenks and family were the only bright spots in this book. Can we get a spin-off with them? Maybe there is one. I will investigate. Jenks has more heart, more intelligence, than either Rachel or Ivy. And I love hearing about how pixies and fairies have been warring for centuries. I am way more interested in them, then the witches, vampires, and demons running around in this book.<br /> <br />Nick who I was rooting for initially, is just as dumb as Rachel. (Spoilers for book one) In the last book Rachel found out that brainiac was summoning a demon. Because of this they both have demon marks on them due to Nick using the demon to save Rachel and the marks are seen as debts until repaid. Well we find out that Nick is still trying to learn from the demon and get it to do what he wants. <br /> <br />And Rachel who has the common sense God gave a gnat knows this is a bad idea but you know, just kind of sits back and let's Nick do what he wants. Because of a mess-up because neither of these two are intelligent, there is a change to Nick and Rachel's relationship. The book leaves things up in the air, however, I don't care enough to see if they work it out.<br /> <br />Trent from the last book is the only other character besides Jenks that I liked. Readers know (spoilers for book one) that Trent was behind a death in the last book. However, he's not an idiot and we find out what has actually been going on and it links back to the goings on in book one.<br /> <br />The world building got a bit clunkier in this book. I think the problem was there were too many creatures to keep track of and what their triggers were. We had weres, vampires, pixies, demons, witches, etc. We also had some explanations of ley lines, and familiars. After a while I felt like I was being force fed an instruction book on witchcraft and got bored. <br /> <br />The flow from chapter to chapter was a bit off in places too, and I think that things would have been better if there had only been that one plot that may have led to some revelations, but not everything that was thrown at us in this book. <br /> <br />I have no further urge to read what happens in the Hollows. I am sure that somehow Rachel will get bitten by Ivy. Rachel will apologize for it. Rachel is probably going to end up with someone totally unsuited for her. And she will almost die like a million times. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10172521332867536926" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/43056599?book_show_action=true">Jan 14, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristy" href="/user/show/1495722-kristy">Kristy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer43056599" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer523535127751293418">Okay this book was a better than the first but it really took me a lot longer than is typical for me to get through the first half of the book. I don't know what Kim Harrison is trying to do in her writing but the first half of her books are really tedious and boring. You make it through it and the second half is interesting, exciting, full of suspence. I wish she'd put as much effort in the first half of her books as she does in the second.<br/><br/>Rachel seems to be a more rounded character in this boo</span>
  <span id="freeText523535127751293418" style="display:none">Okay this book was a better than the first but it really took me a lot longer than is typical for me to get through the first half of the book. I don't know what Kim Harrison is trying to do in her writing but the first half of her books are really tedious and boring. You make it through it and the second half is interesting, exciting, full of suspence. I wish she'd put as much effort in the first half of her books as she does in the second.<br /><br />Rachel seems to be a more rounded character in this book although she can still be annoying at times. Her supporting characters are taking shape better and I'm enjoying having some mysteries solved. There is no point in not having at least one or two problems solved in a book series. I always feel led on like a soap opera if there isn't some closure in a book.<br /><br />I'm interested enough in picking up a couple more books to see how this story goes. I have a feeling I'll be wading through the first half of the next book to get to the real story again but I guess I'll just have to wait and see.</span>

<div id="review_102417391" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/102417391" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3344685-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1388694025p2/3344685.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/102417391?book_show_action=true">Jul 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/3344685-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007236114" href="/book/show/588943.The_Good_The_Bad_and_The_Undead">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=books-i-own-print">books-i-own-print</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=books-i-own-kindle">books-i-own-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=read-before-goodreads">read-before-goodreads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer102417391" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12135695215508128854"><b>1st read - 2009</b><br/><b>2nd read - July 2017</b><br/><b>3rd read - June 2020</b><br/><br/>I read the first few books in this series years ago but it was only when I started my reread recently that I remembered how much I enjoyed this world. Rachel isn't perfect but she's a great character because she's so flawed. She makes stupid mistakes and she's far too trusting but she's learning and I'm hoping she won't keep repeating the same errors over and over again. I'm enjoying seeing her learn more about the magic she is capable of, s</span>
  <span id="freeText12135695215508128854" style="display:none"><b>1st read - 2009</b><br /><b>2nd read - July 2017</b><br /><b>3rd read - June 2020</b><br /><br />I read the first few books in this series years ago but it was only when I started my reread recently that I remembered how much I enjoyed this world. Rachel isn't perfect but she's a great character because she's so flawed. She makes stupid mistakes and she's far too trusting but she's learning and I'm hoping she won't keep repeating the same errors over and over again. I'm enjoying seeing her learn more about the magic she is capable of, she came across as a fairly mediocre witch in the beginning but it looks like  she has more power than she realised. We learn a bit more about her background and a connection between her family and Trent's which I think is extremely interesting. Trent's character definitely has me intrigued, he has a bad side but I'm starting to wonder if he's not quite as evil as first suspected.<br /><br />I think my main pet peeve in this book was her boyfriend Nick who, lets face it, is a bit of a wet blanket and I have absolutely zero idea what Rachel sees in him - especially considering all the lies and secrets he's keeping. The other thing that gets on my last nerve is her relationship with vampire Ivy. The two are supposed to be friends and business partners but their relationship presses all my buttons in the completely wrong way. I get that the author is trying to show that vampires are dangerous but Ivy crosses so many lines that it's just not funny. Their relationship feels abusive to me, there are many times Ivy either can't or won't take no for an answer and Rachel is constantly making excuses for her. What's even worse is that Rachel then blames herself for doing things that triggered Ivy's "vampire instincts" and that really rubs me up the wrong way. If you had a male character who acted the way Ivy does then I think a lot of people would be really angry about the way the situation was handled and it's probably the main thing that makes me reticent to continue the series.<br /><br />Having said that there is a lot to love about these books so I'm going to push through and hope Ivy  either has a serious attitude adjustment or that someone stakes her and puts me out of my misery! Jenks and his family are brilliant, I already mentioned my love for Rachel and curiosity about Trent and I'm also kind of curious about Big Al too. He's got the better of Rachel every time they've met so far and she's in a whole heap of trouble because of that but I can't help wanting to see how she gets herself out of it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12135695215508128854" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_527142437" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/527142437" />
    <a title="Jane Stewart" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3789528-jane-stewart"><img alt="Jane Stewart" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1346001994p2/3789528.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/527142437?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jane Stewart" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jane Stewart" href="/user/show/3789528-jane-stewart">Jane Stewart</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781400134724" href="/book/show/1352200.The_Good_the_Bad_and_the_Undead">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3789528-jane-stewart?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer527142437" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2763586143389033325">Heroine’s recklessness and mistakes get her into trouble which is too close to stupidity for me.<br/><br/>If you like to lose yourself in an urban fantasy world, this is a good one. But I want stories where character and plot are the main draws. Here not much happens to support the plot. The setting has a wide variety of paranormals: witches, vampires, pixies, elves, werewolves, and demons. I like the way they live, work, and interact with each other and humans in current day.<br/><br/>My biggest problem is that I </span>
  <span id="freeText2763586143389033325" style="display:none">Heroine’s recklessness and mistakes get her into trouble which is too close to stupidity for me.<br /><br />If you like to lose yourself in an urban fantasy world, this is a good one. But I want stories where character and plot are the main draws. Here not much happens to support the plot. The setting has a wide variety of paranormals: witches, vampires, pixies, elves, werewolves, and demons. I like the way they live, work, and interact with each other and humans in current day.<br /><br />My biggest problem is that I don’t enjoy Rachel. She is reckless, impulsive, jumps to wrong conclusions, and makes mistakes. Those character traits are the source of her troubles and conflicts throughout the book. Some of it is stupid. In one scene she tells Trent she doesn’t like him because he is a thief (and other things). Well, Rachel is a thief in this book which bothered me. A thinks B stole a fish. Rachel is hired to steal it back which she does. Then she finds out A was mistaken and B did not steal the fish. So I think Rachel should return the fish to B. She does not. She keeps the fish for herself. Yes ornery characters can be fun. In fact I love some of them in other books, but this didn’t work for me. I couldn’t like her, and therefore I could not enjoy her escapades.<br /><br />Other Rachel examples:<br />A wants to take one of Rachel’s books. Rachel says “Let him have it.” After A leaves, B tells Rachel now she cannot do the spell she needs because it was in that book. Rachel says “Oh.”<br /><br />Rachel is in a dangerous situation and needs to do a chant. She gets distracted in the middle of the chant and says “Oh my God,” then she forgets the last word of the chant, but she has already interrupted the chant, then several moments later she remembers the last word.<br /><br />Another problem:<br />In every crisis, someone else comes along to save Rachel - at least in the first two books. She may do something weird trying to save herself, but it doesn’t finish the scene. It reminds me of “deus ex machina” (a god comes in to move the story forward when the writer can’t think of another way out).<br /><br />The narrator Marguerite Gavin was ok.<br /><br />THE HOLLOWS (RACHEL MORGAN) SERIES:<br />As of 2013 there are 11 books in the series. Sadly it’s not for me, but I gave it a try. The three I read are:<br />3 stars. Dead Witch Walking, Book 1<br />2 stars. The Good, the Bad, and the Undead, Book 2<br />1 star. Pale Demon, Book 9<br /><br />DATA:<br />Narrative mode: 1st person Rachel. Unabridged audiobook length: 14 hrs and 22 mins. Swearing language: moderate but rarely used. Sexual language: none. Number of sex scenes: one briefly referred to. Setting: time similar to current day Cincinnati, Ohio. Book copyright: 2005. Genre: urban fantasy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2763586143389033325" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Kira" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7247640-kira"><img alt="Kira" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1395614362p2/7247640.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/250958684?book_show_action=true">Dec 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kira" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kira" href="/user/show/7247640-kira">Kira</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7247640-kira?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7247640-kira?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7247640-kira?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer250958684" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1225859316422162811">Witches are being murdered. The FIB asks Rachel to help with the case. Rachel is convinced Trent is behind the murders. But things get complicated along the way, and Rachel has some run ins with vampires and demons.<br/><br/>I think this book is an improvement over the first one, but it’s not significantly better. I don’t like the way vampires are depicted in this series. There isn’t much good in them. They are depicted as dangerous and easily unhinged. But the danger comes with strong sexual vibes that d</span>
  <span id="freeText1225859316422162811" style="display:none">Witches are being murdered. The FIB asks Rachel to help with the case. Rachel is convinced Trent is behind the murders. But things get complicated along the way, and Rachel has some run ins with vampires and demons.<br /><br />I think this book is an improvement over the first one, but it’s not significantly better. I don’t like the way vampires are depicted in this series. There isn’t much good in them. They are depicted as dangerous and easily unhinged. But the danger comes with strong sexual vibes that don’t sit right with me. With Ivy it never feels like it’s just about the blood; she wants sex too or at least that’s how it seems to me. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Ivy comes close to making Rachel her scion against her will. Rachel views the entire situation as her fault for triggering Ivy’s vampire instincts even though basically being alive and around a vampire sets them off. Later in the book Ivy becomes Piscary’s scion against her will, and Rachel views it as rape. I hate it that the two situations are viewed as extremely different when they are very similar. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Ivy is a much better person than Piscary, but the good she does for Rachel doesn’t outweigh the harm she causes especially after Ivy’s secrets are revealed. Rachel is in denial when it comes to Ivy. She only sees what she wants to, which is admirable in some ways because she overlooks Ivy’s many faults. However she is the victim but doesn’t view herself as one and blames herself for what happens with Ivy because of her familiarity with her. The whole situation is very frustrating. <br /><br />More hints were dropped about Rachel being more powerful than normal. Some interesting things were learned about her family history. As much as I like Rachel, she is immature. The way she acted while working on an important FIB case proved it. Trent was much more palatable although nothing he did made up for the bad things he did in the last book. He’s still one of my favorite characters though. Al is a great gray character because his motives are completely unknown at this point. Piscary was everything I thought he’d be. Nick is someone I find hard to like. He gives Rachel good advice but I don’t trust him.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1225859316422162811" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_92745786" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/92745786" />
    <a title="Celine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3387843-celine"><img alt="Celine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460292659p2/3387843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/92745786?book_show_action=true">Mar 06, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Celine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Celine" href="/user/show/3387843-celine">Celine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3387843-celine?shelf=werewolves-shifters">werewolves-shifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3387843-celine?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3387843-celine?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3387843-celine?shelf=wizardy-magic">wizardy-magic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer92745786" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15535103047003237561"><b>Review of third read</b><br/><br/>I rarely truly binge. I am often a restless person, someone who gets up after reading for an hour, someone who will watch ten TV shows halfway through the season, rarely finishing any of them. Even when I <i>love</i> a series, or a book, or whatever, the odds are slim of me following it up in any consistent way.<br/><br/>Which I why I find it fascinating that I read two Hollows books right after each other without a second of unrest or boredom. No need to pick up another novel in between. Kim</span>
  <span id="freeText15535103047003237561" style="display:none"><b>Review of third read</b><br /><br />I rarely truly binge. I am often a restless person, someone who gets up after reading for an hour, someone who will watch ten TV shows halfway through the season, rarely finishing any of them. Even when I <i>love</i> a series, or a book, or whatever, the odds are slim of me following it up in any consistent way.<br /><br />Which I why I find it fascinating that I read two Hollows books right after each other without a second of unrest or boredom. No need to pick up another novel in between. Kim Harrison writes so wonderfully smoothly - her scenes flow into the other, her character's banter fueling the pace in moments where plot takes a back seat. Most of the characters are flawed, well-rounded, and fully themselves. The triad at the core of the series, witch Rachel, pixie Jenks, and vampire Ivy, balance each other in interesting ways. Their family bond (though they don't see it yet as one) is what makes me return to these books. It scratches an itch that TV shows such as Friends and Gilmore Girls do as well - a group of people that care for each other, not romantically involved, and who always stand up for each other at the end of the day.<br /><br />Finally, I think Ms Harrison has done a great job on Trent. Reckless businessman, mobster, and all-round mysterious, he is the character I find most intriguing. His collected manner is a fantastic foil to Rachel's fiery temper, and he is deliciously evil yet vulnerable. I never read the last few books of this series, and I am now looking forward to see more of his layers peeled away.<br /><br /><b>Review of second read</b><br /><br />In honour of the release of Pale Demon, the ninth book in the Hollows series, on the 22rd this month I'm rereading the whole series.<br /><br />When I first read these book I didn't even know the "urban fantasy" was a genre and I devoured these books, enjoying every bit of them. They introduced me to this wonderful world where humans, vampires, werewolves and witches all live together in a contemporary world. Every detail about this world was new for me, never having read anything like it.<br /><br />And even though my innocent fascination is gone after reading my share of urban fantasy, this series is in my opinion one of the best out there. It has the right mix of fast-paced action, suspense, true friendships, drama, character development and even some romance to keep the story interesting.<br /><br />In this book the FIB (the investigation bureau for non-Inderlanders, also known as those boring human beings) contracts white earth witch Rachel to help find something or someone that's killing ley line witches one after the other. The trail leads to extremely rich and attractive young bachelor Trent Kalamack, that also runs most of Cincinatti's underground. But as always, nothing is what it seems...<br /><br />Rachel is flawed, but that makes her so much easier to relate to. She doesn't always make the right decisions and is extremely stubborn at times which makes me love her even more. She cares about her family and her close friends/business partners and she tries to make the best out of everything. Throughout the series we see her struggling with her morals. What is the line between good and bad? In this book she starts to realise not everything is black and white. Even though she has sworn never to deal with demons (as people who are stupid enough to do that usually end up dead or worse) the smut on her soul is only increasing. And what to do about that demon-summoning boyfriend?<br /><br />These books are quite long (about 450 pages in paperback) you read through them at an incredible speed. I like reading about how Rachel deals with her blood-craving living vampire roommate, her delicate relation with the FIB, the investigation part of the story. Kim Harrison's writing is clear and adds to the story, describing the witch spells and other magic in detail.<br /><br />I would also like to give Ms. Harrison credit of her incredible cast of secondary characters. They all have their distinct personalities, and I love them all for that. Especially the mysterious Trent is awesome, and the tongue-in-cheek pixy Jenks is hilarious.<br /><br />Even if you've already know where the story is going these books are extremely engrossing. I would recommend them to everyone interested in paranormal stories. Even if the books take some time to get into at the start, they are totally worth it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15535103047003237561" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_871235619" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/871235619" />
    <a title="Marianne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16417346-marianne"><img alt="Marianne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528189144p2/16417346.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/871235619?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marianne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marianne" href="/user/show/16417346-marianne">Marianne</a>
      </span>
